- Pre-FOMC drift window screen: rejected before implementation as a density-aware follow-up to the previously rejected exact scheduled-macro event screen. Source reviewed: Lucca and Moench (2015), "The Pre-FOMC Announcement Drift", Journal of Finance 70(1), plus official Federal Reserve FOMC historical meeting pages and current FOMC calendar `https://www.federalreserve.gov/monetarypolicy/fomccalendars.htm`. Result path: `/private/tmp/pre_fomc_window_screen_top.csv`; ES scratch cache: `/private/tmp/es_rth_wide.parquet`. The no-write screen parsed 133 scheduled FOMC statement dates from 2010 through 2026, excluding unscheduled/cancelled/conference-call/notation-vote historical rows, then tested known-in-advance meeting-day, pre-meeting, and post-meeting trading-day windows such as `pre_1_to_5`, `pre_1_to_10`, `pre_1_to_15`, and `pre_1_to_20` across Apex-compatible same-day ES RTH holds. It tested 280 rows and found zero pass-shaped rows and zero near rows. Exact meeting-day long 09:35-12:00 had WFA PF 1.521 and MAR 0.297 but only 83 WFA trades, while broader pre-meeting windows reached density but were flat or negative after costs; for example `pre_1_to_20` long 11:00-16:00 had WFA n1,596/PF 1.016/MAR 0.023/expectancy R 0.007 and incubation n239/PF 1.122/MAR 0.572. Rejected because the deterministic pre-FOMC drift translation cannot satisfy both WFA trade density and WFA PF/MAR/expectancy gates in ES intraday RTH form; do not revisit scheduled-policy timing unless using a materially different source variable, not just wider event windows.
- ICI weekly mutual-fund/ETF flow pressure source audit: rejected before implementation at the data-access gate after the user allowed reliable real-time external datasets. Source reviewed: Investment Company Institute weekly estimated flow pages, including `https://www.ici.org/topics/weekly-estimated-flow-reports`, `https://www.ici.org/research/stats/flows`, and `https://www.ici.org/research/stats/combined_flows`. The thesis would have used public weekly estimated domestic-equity mutual fund and ETF net flows, shifted by at least one full week after the week-ended Wednesday reference date, as a no-hindsight demand-flow state for ES RTH holds. The current/recent annual files such as `https://www.ici.org/flows_data_2025.xls`, `https://www.ici.org/flows_data_2026.xls`, `https://www.ici.org/combined_flows_data_2025.xls`, and `https://www.ici.org/combined_flows_data_2026.xls` are directly downloadable, but old annual files for 2010/2014/2020/2024 return 404 and the historical files listed on the weekly-flow reports page, including `/statistical-report/combined_flows_data_hist_2026.xls`, `/statistical-report/flows_data_hist_2026.xls`, and `/statistical-report/etf_flows_data_hist_2026.xls`, are marked as disabled/member-login reports in the page markup and direct requests return 403. Rejected because there is no reliable public historical data path spanning WFA and incubation; do not use ICI flows for an acceptance candidate unless a documented licensed/member data path or another point-in-time public archive is added.
- Month-end stock-bond rebalancing pressure screen: rejected before implementation. Source family reviewed: month-end target-allocation/pension-fund and target-date-fund rebalancing literature, including Mazzoleni and Melone, "The Unintended Consequences of Rebalancing" (NBER working paper 33554), plus the prior turn-of-month/rebalancing evidence already audited. Scratch result paths: `/private/tmp/month_end_stock_bond_rebalance_screen_top.csv` and `/private/tmp/month_end_stock_bond_rebalance_screen_all.csv`; raw ETF cache: `/private/tmp/yahoo_stock_bond_rebalance_cache.csv`; ES scratch cache: `/private/tmp/es_rth_wide.parquet`. Stooq was rejected as an unattended data path because its CSV endpoints required browser proof-of-work/API-key/CAPTCHA handling; Yahoo chart data for SPY/TLT/IEF were used only for this no-write audit, and any promotion would require a documented production market-data source with reliable adjusted daily histories. The screen used adjusted SPY/TLT/IEF closes from 2009-12-01 through 2026-06-01, shifted all ETF signals to the prior close before ES entries, then tested month-end/turn-of-month states conditioned on stock-vs-bond month-to-date and prior-month imbalances across Apex-compatible RTH windows. It tested 116,342 rows and found zero pass-shaped rows and zero near rows. Best dense rows improved over generic calendar exposure but stayed below WFA gates: `turn_last5_first5` with `spy_ief_mtd_diff <= 0.0`, long 11:00-15:30, had WFA n500/PF 1.366/MAR 0.369/expectancy R 0.156 and incubation n65/PF 1.374/MAR 0.878; `turn_last5_first5` with `spy_ief_mtd_diff_rank60 <= 0.4`, long 11:00-15:30, had WFA n542/PF 1.361/MAR 0.418/expectancy R 0.157 and incubation n72/PF 1.436/MAR 0.967; `first_7td` with `spy_ief_mtd_diff_z60 <= 0.0`, long 11:00-15:30, cleared incubation at n78/PF 1.676/MAR 1.652 but failed WFA at n531/PF 1.360/MAR 0.306/expectancy R 0.155. High-PF rows were underdense event artifacts. Rejected because stock-bond month-end rebalancing conditioning does not satisfy WFA PF/MAR/expectancy and incubation density under current costs; do not rerun as a simple stock-bond month-end/turn-window variant without materially new evidence.
- Official Cboe VIX futures term-structure screen: rejected before implementation. Source reviewed: Lee (2017), "Investors' Heterogeneity in Beliefs, the VIX Futures Basis, and S&P 500 Index Futures Returns", Journal of Futures Markets, DOI `10.1002/fut.21838`, plus VIX-futures term-structure timing evidence from Fassas-style market-timing papers. Official data came from Cboe's CFE historical data API/list endpoint and CDN contract files, e.g. `https://www-api.cboe.com/us/futures/market_statistics/historical_data/product/list/VX/` and `https://cdn.cboe.com/data/us/futures/market_statistics/historical_data/VX/VX_YYYY-MM-DD.csv`; Cboe's aggregate daily volume/open-interest CSV at `https://cdn.cboe.com/data/us/futures/market_statistics/historical_data/cfevoloi.csv` was also verified as downloadable. Scratch script: `/private/tmp/vix_futures_term_structure_screen.py`; result paths: `/private/tmp/vix_futures_term_structure_screen_top.csv` and `/private/tmp/vix_futures_term_structure_screen_all.csv`; raw normalized cache: `/private/tmp/cboe_vx_futures_daily_cache.parquet`; ES cache: `/private/tmp/es_rth_wide.parquet`. The no-write screen downloaded monthly VX/VXT contract CSVs from 2013 through 2026, built front/second/third monthly VX settlement, volume, open-interest, days-to-expiry, contango, curve, return, change, rank, and z-score features, and shifted every CFE settlement by one ES session so no same-day settlement was used before RTH entries. It tested 45,990 fixed-threshold/window rows across Apex-compatible RTH holds and found zero pass-shaped rows and zero near rows. The best WFA-PF row was too sparse: `vx1_vol_z126 >= 1.5`, short 14:30-16:00, had WFA n228/PF 1.568/MAR 0.489/expectancy R 0.242 and incubation n38/PF 2.127/MAR 2.310. Dense rows were recent-holdout artifacts rather than WFA edges: `vx1_ret1_rank63 >= 0.7`, long 09:35-15:30, had WFA n812/PF 1.053/MAR 0.056/expectancy R 0.026 while incubation was strong at n118/PF 2.073/MAR 4.319. Rejected because official VX futures term-structure information is reliable and point-in-time with a one-session lag, but it does not meet WFA PF/MAR/expectancy or incubation density gates for ES intraday execution under current costs; do not rerun as a VIX-futures-contango or VX-basis variant without materially new structure.
- Official Cboe aggregate VIX-futures activity screen: rejected before implementation after the external-data allowance. Source reviewed: VIX-futures basis/activity timing literature, using the official Cboe CFE aggregate daily volume/open-interest CSV `https://cdn.cboe.com/data/us/futures/market_statistics/historical_data/cfevoloi.csv`. Scratch scripts/results: `/private/tmp/cboe_vx_activity_screen.py`, `/private/tmp/cboe_vx_activity_screen_top.csv`, `/private/tmp/cboe_vx_activity_targeted_top.csv`, `/private/tmp/cboe_vx_activity_fine_top.csv`, `/private/tmp/cboe_vx_activity_path_screen.py`, and `/private/tmp/cboe_vx_activity_path_top.csv`; raw cache: `/private/tmp/cboe_cfevoloi.csv`; ES caches: `/private/tmp/es_rth_wide.parquet` plus active-roll Databento 1-minute paths. The no-write fixed-window screens shifted each CFE daily observation by one ES session, tested aggregate VX total volume, total open interest, volume/OI ratio, changes, ranks, and z-scores against Apex-compatible RTH windows, and then ran a narrow managed-path audit on the strongest low-open-interest late-day long cluster with stop-first 1-minute stop/target handling. The broad fixed screen tested 49,344 rows with zero pass-shaped rows and one near row; the best was `vx_total_oi_rank63 <= 0.10`, long 13:30-15:30, with WFA n450/PF 1.460/MAR 0.461/expectancy R 0.214 and incubation n76/PF 1.384/MAR 1.256. The fine fixed grid tested 65,790 rows with zero pass-shaped rows and 906 near rows; representative near rows were `z63 <= -1.25`, long 13:30-15:45, with WFA n499/PF 1.486/MAR 0.846/expectancy R 0.220 and incubation n93/PF 1.513/MAR 2.410, and denser `z50 <= -1.125`, long 13:30-15:45, with WFA n594/PF 1.405/MAR 0.807/expectancy R 0.189 and incubation n98/PF 1.714/MAR 3.344. The managed-path audit tested 291,060 rows and found zero pass-shaped rows; the best score remained `z63 <= -1.275`, long 13:30-15:45 with `stop_pct=0.012` and `target_r=2.0`, at WFA n486/PF 1.495/MAR 0.879/expectancy R 0.225, core n98/PF 2.494, and incubation n91/PF 1.577/MAR 2.602. Rows with enough WFA density diluted below the PF gate, e.g. `rank42 <= 0.15`, long 13:30-15:30 with `stop_pct=0.012` and `target_r=2.0`, had WFA n573/PF 1.452/MAR 0.696/expectancy R 0.214 with solid core/incubation. Rejected because official Cboe aggregate VX activity is reliable point-in-time data with a conservative one-session lag, but the edge still cannot clear WFA trade count and PF together under current costs; do not rerun as a low-VX-open-interest or VIX-futures-activity late-day long variant without materially new structure.
- Federal Reserve H.4.1 weekly liquidity-state screen: rejected before implementation after the external-data allowance. Source reviewed: Federal Reserve balance-sheet/liquidity state and intermediary-risk-capacity literature; the official H.4.1 release page says the data are generally released Thursday at 4:30 p.m., and data came from public FRED mirrors of official H.4.1 weekly series for total Fed assets (`WALCL`), reserve balances (`WRESBAL`), and Treasury General Account (`WTREGEN`). Scratch script/result paths: `/private/tmp/fed_h41_liquidity_screen.py`, `/private/tmp/fed_h41_liquidity_screen_top.csv`, and `/private/tmp/fed_h41_liquidity_screen_all.csv`; raw cache: `/private/tmp/fed_h41_liquidity_cache.csv`. The daily RRP FRED graph endpoint timed out repeatedly from shell/Python, so it was not used. The weekly H.4.1 files were downloaded with `curl`, covered 2002-12-18 through 2026-06-03, and every Wednesday observation was made tradable only from Friday RTH or later. The screen built 329 lagged features from assets, reserves, TGA, net-liquidity proxy (`WALCL - WTREGEN`), reserves-minus-TGA, reserves/assets, and TGA/assets; then it tested 138,656 fixed-threshold/window rows across Apex-compatible same-day ES RTH holds. It found zero pass-shaped rows and only three near rows. The best near rows were long ES after high reserves-minus-TGA states or increases: `reserves_minus_tga_rank13 >= 0.90`, long 09:35-15:30, had WFA n566/PF 1.353/MAR 0.549/expectancy R 0.153 and incubation n71/PF 1.317/MAR 1.095; `reserves_minus_tga_diff13 >= 237951`, long 11:00-15:30, had WFA n511/PF 1.393/MAR 0.824/expectancy R 0.174 and incubation n86/PF 1.196/MAR 0.454; `reserves_minus_tga_diff26 >= 363012`, long 11:00-13:30, had WFA n452/PF 1.369/MAR 0.542/expectancy R 0.152 and incubation n85/PF 1.108/MAR 0.280. Rejected because weekly Fed liquidity state is usable with conservative lag, but the ES intraday edge remains below WFA PF/expectancy and incubation MAR/economics; do not rerun as a simple Fed-balance-sheet/reserves/TGA liquidity-state variant without adding a materially different source variable such as a reliable official daily RRP feed.
- Chicago Fed NFCI financial-conditions screen: rejected before implementation as a distinct official financial-conditions follow-up. Source reviewed: Federal Reserve Bank of Chicago National Financial Conditions Index and financial-stress expected-return literature. Raw data came from the FRED graph CSV for `NFCI`, cached at `/private/tmp/fred_NFCI.csv`; scratch script/results: `/private/tmp/nfci_financial_conditions_screen.py`, `/private/tmp/nfci_financial_conditions_screen_top.csv`, and `/private/tmp/nfci_financial_conditions_screen_all.csv`. The screen treated each Friday NFCI observation as tradable only from the next Friday RTH session, then tested NFCI level, one-/four-/13-/26-/52-week changes and means, ranks, and z-scores across Apex-compatible same-day ES RTH holds. It tested 40,656 rows and found zero pass-shaped rows and zero near rows. The highest-PF rows were underdense, such as `nfci_diff1_z104 <= -1.5`, long 09:35-13:30, with WFA n171/PF 1.800/MAR 1.220 and incubation n14, or `nfci_diff1_z52 <= -1.5`, long 09:35-15:30, with WFA n187/PF 1.979/MAR 0.991 and incubation n19. Dense rows were not economically strong enough: for example `nfci_diff1_rank104 <= 0.4`, long 09:35-16:00, had WFA n1004/PF 1.220/MAR 0.514/expectancy R 0.099 and core PF only 1.074, while `nfci_diff1_z13 <= 0.0`, long 11:00-16:00, had WFA n1231/PF 1.248/MAR 0.394/expectancy R 0.110 and core PF only 1.012. - Official credit/default-spread data-source audit: rejected before implementation at the data gate. Source reviewed: default-spread and credit-risk expected-return literature. The intended source variables were public FRED graph CSV series for ICE BofA high-yield OAS (`BAMLH0A0HYM2`), broad corporate OAS (`BAMLC0A0CM`), Moody Baa-minus-10Y (`BAA10Y`), and Aaa-minus-10Y (`AAA10Y`). Direct downloads of the two ICE BofA OAS series succeeded only with a 2023-06-09 start date, leaving no usable WFA history. Direct 60-second downloads of `BAA10Y` and `AAA10Y` repeatedly timed out with zero bytes received. Rejected because no unattended public data path currently supplies enough reliable, long-history credit-spread observations for a no-hindsight ES acceptance candidate; do not use this branch unless a licensed/official historical feed or responsive FRED endpoint is added.
- New York Fed ACM Treasury term-premium data-source audit: rejected before implementation at the no-hindsight data gate. Source reviewed: Adrian, Crump, and Moench (2013), "Pricing the Term Structure with Linear Regressions", Journal of Financial Economics, and the New York Fed Treasury Term Premia page. The page exposes `/medialibrary/media/research/data_indicators/acmPlot_data.csv` and `https://www.newyorkfed.org/medialibrary/media/research/data_indicators/ACMTermPremium.xls`; scratch downloads: `/private/tmp/nyfed_acmPlot_data.csv` and `/private/tmp/ACMTermPremium.xls`. The CSV is monthly only, while the Excel workbook contains a daily `ACM Daily` sheet from 1961-06-14 through the latest month with fitted yields, term premia, and risk-neutral yields for maturities 1-10. However, the NY Fed notes that the ACM model is re-estimated once a month and this can change historical decompositions of Treasury yields. Without point-in-time vintage workbooks, a backtest using the current daily sheet would see revised historical term-premium estimates that were not necessarily available on each trade date. Rejected before screening because the public current workbook is not a reliable no-hindsight dataset for acceptance; revisit only if archived monthly ACM vintage files or another point-in-time term-premium source are available.

Source reviewed: official Office of Financial Research FSI page `https://www.financialresearch.gov/financial-stress-index/`, which describes the OFR FSI as a daily market-based stress snapshot and states that it publishes data current from two business days prior. The fixed-window scan tested 249,480 rows and found zero pass-shaped rows and three near rows. Best fixed row was `other_advanced_economies_diff21_rank21 <= 0.20`, long 09:35-16:00, with WFA n700/PF 1.380/MAR 0.490/expectancy R 0.170 versus required MAR 0.622, and incubation n84/PF 1.530/MAR 1.476/expectancy R 0.189. A narrow stop-first managed-path audit around the near clusters tested 5,292 rows with zero pass-shaped rows and 11 near rows; best managed row was the same stress-reversal cluster, long 10:00-16:00 with `stop_pct=0.010` and `target_r=1.0`, at WFA n700/PF 1.353/MAR 0.458/expectancy R 0.153 and incubation n84/PF 1.558/MAR 1.643/expectancy R 0.226. Rejected because OFR FSI is reliable and real-time-usable with conservative two-business-day lag, but the edge cannot meet WFA PF/MAR/expectancy under current costs; do not rerun as a renamed official-financial-stress, safe-asset-stress, or global-stress reversal filter without materially new structure.

- OFR U.S. Money Market Fund Data Release source audit: rejected before implementation at the no-hindsight data gate. Source reviewed: official OFR STFM `mmf` dataset page `https://www.financialresearch.gov/short-term-funding-monitor/datasets/mmf/` and API endpoint `https://data.financialresearch.gov/v1/series/dataset?dataset=mmf`. The endpoint is public and returned 42 monthly series; most aggregate series span 2010-11-30 through 2026-04-30, while the shorter manager-year subset starts in 2016. However, the series metadata for the 2010-start aggregates explicitly lists `vintage_approach` and `vintage` as `Monthly Revisions - Complete Series`, and the release is based on SEC Form N-MFP filings plus OFR mappings. Rejected because the current OFR API would use revised historical series and mappings without point-in-time vintages. - OFR Hedge Fund Monitor SEC Form PF source audit: rejected before implementation at the no-hindsight data gate. Source reviewed: official OFR Hedge Fund Monitor API page `https://www.financialresearch.gov/hedge-fund-monitor/api/` and dataset endpoint `https://data.financialresearch.gov/hf/v1/series/dataset?dataset=fpf`. The default endpoint returned 329 quarterly SEC Form PF aggregate hedge-fund series from 2013-03-31 through 2025-12-31, but metadata labels the data `Current vintage, as of last update`; documented `vintage=f`, `vintage=p`, and `vintage=a` dataset requests returned HTTP 502 from the public API during the audit. Rejected because the available public aggregate history is current-vintage only and not reconstructible point-in-time from this endpoint. Do not use OFR Form PF hedge-fund aggregates unless the API vintage requests are repaired and release lags are modeled, or raw Form PF aggregates are available as point-in-time vintages.

- New York Fed overnight reverse-repo liquidity screen: rejected before implementation after confirming the official daily source path is usable. Rejected because short-term-reversal factor spillover is below WFA PF/MAR/expectancy and overlaps the already rejected factor-spillover/prior-reversal families without improving the pass shape; do not rerun as simple ST reversal factor rank, ST_REV z-score, or daily short-term-reversal factor state without materially new structure.

- Moving-average filter / crossover trend-following audit: rejected before implementation after user review. Source checked: Edward Olszewski (2001), "A strategy for trading the S&P 500 futures market", Journal of Economics and Finance 25(1), DOI `10.1007/BF02759687`; this is adjacent to the already staged-and-rejected `daily_time_series_momentum` campaign based on Moskowitz, Ooi, and Pedersen (2012). Scratch result paths: `/private/tmp/ma_trend_following_flat_screen_top.csv` and `/private/tmp/ma_trend_following_flat_screen_all.csv`; ES cache used: `/private/tmp/es_rth_wide.parquet`. The no-write screen used only completed prior RTH closes, then tested classic price-vs-SMA filters, MA/EMA crossovers, long-flat/short-flat/two-sided modes, 20/40/60/100/200-session windows, 5/10/20/40/60/100/200 crossover pairs, and high-volatility filters from prior 40-session realized-volatility ranks across Apex-compatible same-day ES RTH holds. Rejected because the apparent MA trend-following benefit is a recent/incubation high-volatility long pocket, not a robust full-history ES intraday edge; do not rerun as a simple 40-day/20-day/200-day MA filter, MA crossover, EMA crossover, or high-volatility MA trend-following variant without materially new structure beyond the already failed daily time-series momentum branch.

- ICI aggregate fund-flow / money-market-fund asset source audit: rejected before implementation at the historical data-access gate. Source reviewed: Investment Company Institute weekly estimated long-term mutual fund flows, weekly combined mutual-fund/ETF flows, weekly ETF net issuance, and weekly money-market-fund assets pages. The current public release pages expose recent summary XLS files and tables, but the ICI weekly estimated-flow reports page lists the historical long-term flow and ETF net-issuance XLS reports behind "Login or click here to get access to our Member Statistical Report"; the money-market-fund-assets pages likewise provide recent summary data while full historical reports are member/subscription-gated, and the public release notes say weekly money-market assets for only the last 20 weeks are available. Because the accessible public history is far too short for WFA/incubation and the full historical source requires member/statistical-subscription access, no ES screen was run. Do not reopen as ICI mutual-fund flows, ETF net issuance, combined fund flows, or money-market-fund asset-flow state unless a licensed/approved historical feed with release timing is added.

Features included dollar-volume changes, log dollar volume, Amihud illiquidity, range proxies, signed dollar-pressure, up/down volume pressure, and QQQ/IWM-minus-SPY relative liquidity states, then traded Apex-compatible same-session ES RTH windows through `/private/tmp/es_active_rth_1m_20100606_20260529.parquet` with current ES costs. The bounded screen evaluated 9,940 feature/window rows and found 2,162 positive rows, with zero pass-shaped rows and zero near rows. Best WFA-looking rows failed holdout/incubation: `QQQ_amihud_z63 <= -1.0`, long 13:30-15:30, had full n691/PF 1.230/MAR 0.106, core n89/PF 2.065/MAR 2.997, WFA n498/PF 1.657/MAR 0.809/expectancy R 0.277 versus required WFA density 500, but incubation n61/PF 0.670/MAR -0.528. The denser `qqq_minus_spy_amihud_z21 <= -1.0` sibling had WFA n522/PF 1.685/MAR 0.709 but incubation PF 0.682 and only 73 incubation trades. Rejected because ETF liquidity stress/relief states are core/WFA-useful in pockets but invert or fail in the 2024-2026 holdout; do not rerun as simple SPY/QQQ/IWM ETF dollar-volume, Amihud, range-liquidity, signed-volume, or ETF liquidity-pressure rank/z-score without materially new structure and a production data source.
- Philadelphia Fed ADS real-time business-conditions screen: rejected before implementation after confirming the official ADS page says the index is updated in real time as underlying data are released and that all real-time vintages are available in one file. Source reviewed: Aruoba, Diebold, and Scotti (2009), "Real-Time Measurement of Business Conditions," Journal of Business and Economic Statistics 27(4), pp. 417-27, as referenced by the Philadelphia Fed ADS page. Scratch script/results: `/private/tmp/ads_business_conditions_screen.py`, `/private/tmp/ads_realtime_diagonal.csv`, `/private/tmp/ads_business_conditions_top.csv`, and `/private/tmp/ads_business_conditions_all.csv`; raw official workbook cache: `/private/tmp/ADS_All_Vintages.xlsx`. Best rows were latest-holdout-skewed rather than robust: `ads_mean4_z26 <= -0.5`, long 10:00-13:30, had full n1,338/PF 1.171/MAR 0.116, core n184/PF 1.184/MAR 0.527, WFA n967/PF 1.091/MAR 0.080/expectancy R 0.042 versus required WFA MAR 0.626, and incubation n122/PF 1.835/MAR 3.118. The best WFA-PF rows were too sparse and still weak by MAR/core coverage, e.g. `ads_vol13_z156 <= -1.5`, long 11:00-13:30, had WFA n123/PF 1.526/MAR 0.273, core n8/PF 0.530, and incubation n22. Rejected because real-time ADS macro-state filters improve some recent long-only pockets but miss WFA PF/MAR/expectancy and/or density under point-in-time alignment; do not rerun as simple ADS level, ADS deterioration/improvement, business-conditions rank/z-score, or ADS-volatility regime filter without materially new structure.
- SEC Form 13F ETF institutional-demand screen: rejected before implementation after the external-data allowance as a distinct official point-in-time holdings-flow branch, not a simple EDGAR filing-count rerun. Source reviewed: Gompers and Metrick (2001), "Institutional Investors and Equity Prices," Quarterly Journal of Economics 116(1), DOI `10.1162/003355301556392`, plus official SEC Form 13F Data Sets documentation/page (`https://www.sec.gov/data-research/sec-markets-data/form-13f-data-sets`, data.gov mirror `https://catalog.data.gov/dataset/form-13f-data-sets`). The SEC documentation says the flat files are extracted from EDGAR Form 13F XML filings, include 13F-HR/13F-HR/A/13F-NT forms, and are published quarterly; this audit used only initial `13F-HR` share rows and shifted every filing date by one business day before ES eligibility. Scratch scripts/results: `/private/tmp/sec_13f_etf_demand_screen.py`, `/private/tmp/sec_13f_etf_demand_path_rescue.py`, `/private/tmp/sec_13f_etf_multislot_rescue.py`, `/private/tmp/sec_13f_etf_demand_screen_top.csv`, `/private/tmp/sec_13f_etf_demand_screen_all.csv`, `/private/tmp/sec_13f_etf_demand_path_top.csv`, `/private/tmp/sec_13f_etf_demand_path_all.csv`, `/private/tmp/sec_13f_etf_multislot_top.csv`, and `/private/tmp/sec_13f_etf_multislot_all.csv`; raw/cache paths: `/private/tmp/sec_13f_data_sets`, `/private/tmp/sec_13f_etf_filtered.csv`, and `/private/tmp/sec_13f_etf_daily_features.csv`. The no-write screen downloaded/parsing-cached 53 official SEC 13F packages, filtered to non-option share rows for SPY, QQQ, IWM, IVV, and VOO, yielding 604,754 ETF holding rows from 159,129 filings and 2,735 daily feature rows. It built filing-date ETF holdings, filing counts, new positions, one-/5-/10-/21-/42-day filing aggregates, SPY/QQQ/IWM relative-demand deltas, and rolling rank/z-score features, then tested Apex-compatible ES RTH holds on `/private/tmp/es_active_rth_1m_20100606_20260529.parquet` with current costs. The fixed-window screen evaluated 27,153 rows and found zero pass-shaped rows and 16 near rows. Best fixed row was low one-day IWM-minus-SPY 13F ETF-value delta rank, `iwm_minus_spy_delta_value_sum1_rank63 <= 0.2`, long 10:00-15:30: full n551/PF 1.476/MAR 0.677/expectancy R 0.204, core n78/PF 1.623/MAR 1.953, WFA n453/PF 1.453/MAR 0.609/expectancy R 0.197 versus required MAR 0.65, and incubation n64/PF 1.612/MAR 1.842/expectancy R 0.239. A focused conservative stop-first path rescue over the near cluster evaluated 8,291 rows and found zero pass-shaped rows and 260 near rows; the strongest path-managed row still missed density: `iwm_minus_spy_delta_value_sum1_rank63 <= 0.2`, long 09:35-15:30 with `stop_pct=0.012`, `target_r=1.0`, had WFA n445/PF 1.509/MAR 0.755/expectancy R 0.228, core n77/PF 1.898, and incubation n64/PF 1.623. A two-slot non-overlapping rescue densified the source but diluted WFA economics: 527 rows, zero pass, zero near; best dense row (`rank63 <= 0.15`, long 10:00-13:30 plus 13:30-15:30, `stop_pct=0.010`, `target_r=1.5`) had WFA n708/PF 1.298/MAR 0.482/expectancy R 0.132 despite incubation n112/PF 1.773. Rejected because official 13F ETF institutional-demand shocks are real-time-usable only with filing-date lag but either remain under-dense at acceptable PF/MAR or dilute below the WFA PF/MAR/expectancy gates when densified; do not rerun as simple SPY/QQQ/IWM/IVV/VOO 13F holding, holding-delta, filing-count, new-position, low IWM-minus-SPY demand, high SPY demand, or two-slot 13F ETF-demand timing without materially new structure.
- SEC Form 4 insider transaction pressure screen: rejected before implementation after the external-data allowance as a distinct official point-in-time transaction-content branch, not the prior EDGAR filing-count branch. Source reviewed: Lakonishok and Lee (2001), "Are Insiders' Trades Informative?", Review of Financial Studies 14(1), DOI `10.1093/rfs/14.1.79`, plus official SEC Insider Transactions Data Sets page (`https://www.sec.gov/data-research/sec-markets-data/insider-transactions-data-sets`), which documents quarterly Form 3/4/5 XML-derived data from January 2006 through March 2026. Scratch scripts/results: `/private/tmp/sec_insider_pressure_screen.py`, `/private/tmp/sec_insider_pressure_path_rescue.py`, `/private/tmp/sec_insider_pressure_screen_top.csv`, `/private/tmp/sec_insider_pressure_screen_all.csv`, `/private/tmp/sec_insider_pressure_path_top.csv`, `/private/tmp/sec_insider_pressure_path_all.csv`, `/private/tmp/sec_insider_pressure_gross_value_focus_top.csv`, and `/private/tmp/sec_insider_pressure_gross_value_focus_all.csv`; raw/cache paths: `/private/tmp/sec_insider_data_sets`, `/private/tmp/sec_insider_transactions_filtered.csv`, and `/private/tmp/sec_insider_pressure_daily_features.csv`. The no-write screen downloaded and parsed 81 official SEC quarterly packages, filtered to Form 4 non-derivative open-market purchase/sale rows (`TRANS_CODE` P/S) with positive shares and prices, shifted every filing date by one business day before ES eligibility, and built buy/sell count, dollar value, net/gross pressure, issuer-count, rolling-sum, rank, and z-score features. Fixed-window evaluation produced 3,347,235 transaction rows from 1,220,069 filings, 5,062 daily feature rows, and 16,871 positive fixed rows, with zero pass-shaped and zero near rows. Best fixed dense rows either failed incubation, e.g. low five-day filing z-score short 10:00-13:30 with WFA n507/PF 1.591/MAR 0.652/expectancy R 0.267 but incubation n91/PF 0.802, or failed core/incubation density. A bounded stop-first path rescue over 80 WFA-useful rows found zero pass-shaped rows and six near rows. A focused low-gross-value rescue over 5,607 rows also found zero pass-shaped rows and ten near rows; best was low five-day gross transaction value rank, `gross_value_sum5_rank126 <= 0.20`, long 10:30-15:30 with `stop_pct=0.010`, `target_r=1.5`, full n824/PF 1.333/MAR 0.191, core n124/PF 1.739/MAR 2.937, WFA n688/PF 1.399/MAR 0.657/expectancy R 0.179 versus required WFA PF 1.5 and expectancy R 0.2, and incubation n111/PF 1.176/expectancy R 0.071. Rejected because official Form 4 transaction pressure is reliable and reconstructible with filing-date lag, but simple insider buy/sell pressure, issuer-count spikes, low transaction-gross-value regimes, and low filing-volume regimes cannot satisfy WFA PF/expectancy and incubation economics together; do not rerun as simple SEC insider purchase/sale count, dollar-value imbalance, gross transaction value, issuer-count, filing-count, or Form 4 pressure state without materially new structure.
- FINRA OTC/ATS ETF dark-pool and non-ATS volume source audit: rejected before implementation at the historical data gate. Source reviewed: official FINRA OTC Transparency page, FINRA OTC Transparency API specification, and FINRA Developer API metadata for `weeklySummary`/`weeklySummaryHistoric`. FINRA documents weekly ATS and non-ATS symbol-level volume/trade-count reports, `initialPublishedDate`, and the publication delay for NMS Tier 1 and other securities, so the data would be point-in-time usable with a one-business-day lag after `initialPublishedDate`. Shell probes confirmed the API returns aggregate weekly symbol rows for SPY, QQQ, IWM, IVV, and VOO with `summaryTypeCode` values `ATS_W_SMBL` and `OTC_W_SMBL`; for example the 2026-05-18 partition returned both ATS and OTC aggregate rows for all five ETFs with `initialPublishedDate=2026-06-08`. However, the public `weeklySummary` endpoint returned only 233 weekly rows per ETF from 2021-12-06 through 2026-05-18, and the `weeklySummaryHistoric` partition list covered only 2021-06-14 through 2025-06-02. No ES screen was run because the accessible public history is too short for the repo's default full-history WFA protocol and would early-exit older windows as missing data. Do not reopen as FINRA ATS volume, OTC/non-ATS volume, dark-pool share, SPY/QQQ/IWM off-exchange activity, or symbol-level OTC transparency state unless a full point-in-time archive back to at least the early ES sample is available.
- FINRA TRACE fixed-income market breadth/sentiment source audit: rejected before implementation at the data-access gate. Source reviewed: FINRA Developer metadata for `corporateMarketBreadth`, `corporateMarketSentiment`, `corporate144AMarketBreadth`, `corporate144AMarketSentiment`, `agencyMarketBreadth`, `agencyMarketSentiment`, and `treasuryDailyAggregates`. These datasets would be a plausible official fixed-income-liquidity/credit-risk state source under stock-bond liquidity-linkage literature, but in this environment only metadata was accessible. FINRA partition requests for all seven datasets returned HTTP 401, and direct POST data probes for corporate breadth, corporate sentiment, and Treasury daily aggregates returned `Failed to authenticate, check your authentication token`. No ES screen was run. Do not reopen as TRACE corporate-bond breadth, corporate-bond sentiment, 144A credit-flow, agency-bond breadth, Treasury TRACE aggregate, dealer-customer Treasury volume, or fixed-income market-liquidity state unless FINRA API credentials or an approved public historical export are available.

- Holiday-adjacent / pre-holiday drift screen: rejected before implementation as a deterministic local-data calendar pre-screen. Source reviewed: Ariel (1990), "High Stock Returns before Holidays: Existence and Evidence on Possible Causes", Journal of Finance 45(5), DOI `10.1111/j.1540-6261.1990.tb03731.x`, plus the standing instruction to skip sparse event-only edges unless a pre-screen proves they can reach the 500-trade WFA gate. Scratch script/results: `/private/tmp/holiday_adjacent_screen.py`, `/private/tmp/holiday_adjacent_screen_top.csv`, and `/private/tmp/holiday_adjacent_screen_all.csv`. It evaluated 1,120 rows and found zero pass-shaped rows and zero near rows. The best rows expressed the classic anomaly but were too sparse: `santa_last5_first2` long 14:30-16:00 had full n103/PF 1.730, WFA n61/PF 2.270/MAR 1.047, core n14, and incubation n12; `all_holidays_pre_1` long 13:30-15:30 had full n131/PF 1.233, WFA n82/PF 2.320/MAR 0.474, core n19, and incubation PF 0.201. Broader holiday-week masks improved density only to about WFA n143-165 while diluting economics or failing holdout coverage. Rejected because holiday-adjacent ES drift cannot meet WFA/core/incubation trade-density gates; do not rerun as simple pre-holiday, post-holiday, long-weekend, Santa-rally, Thanksgiving-week, Christmas/New-Year, or generic holiday-week ES timing without materially broader structure.
- NQ calendar-spread activity spillover screen: rejected before implementation as a local Databento 1-minute OHLCV cross-market liquidity/roll-pressure audit. Source framing was the futures volume/rollover activity literature used for the ES calendar-spread activity branch, but this test used completed NQ calendar-spread rows before each ES entry, not ES spread activity or outright NQ participation. The best denser-looking rows still missed economics and/or incubation, e.g. low 63-day NQ spread-total-volume rank long 11:00-16:00 had WFA n184/PF 1.573/MAR 0.381 but only 30 incubation trades with PF 1.004, while high 63-day NQ spread-volume plus weak NQ source return long 11:00-16:00 had WFA n169/PF 1.544/MAR 0.423 and 33 incubation trades. - H.8 commercial-bank credit data retry: still blocked at the no-hindsight data gate. Official ALFRED documentation says vintage dates are required to download data as it existed on past dates and the FRED API requires an `api_key` for observation/vintage requests. Environment audit found no FRED/ALFRED API key. Do not screen or accept H.8 bank-credit, bank-loan, real-estate-loan, or bank-balance-sheet state from single current-vintage FRED/ALFRED graph CSVs; use only if a working point-in-time vintage path or API key is added.
- Volume-clock / transaction-time intraday screen: rejected before implementation as a local 1-minute OHLCV audit. Source framing: Clark (1973), "A Subordinated Stochastic Process Model with Finite Variance for Speculative Prices", Econometrica, DOI `10.2307/1913889`, and Ané and Geman (2000), "Order Flow, Transaction Clock, and Normality of Asset Returns", Journal of Finance, DOI `10.1111/0022-1082.00286`. This was not true bid/ask orderflow and did not use the session's final volume as a signal input. Scratch script/results: `/private/tmp/volume_clock_screen.py`, `/private/tmp/volume_clock_screen_top.csv`, and `/private/tmp/volume_clock_screen_all.csv`. The no-write screen used local active-contract ES RTH 1-minute bars from `/private/tmp/es_active_rth_1m_20100606_20260529.parquet`, computed prior-session 21- and 63-day rolling median total RTH volume as the only volume-clock denominator, then entered only after live cumulative volume crossed completed fractions of that shifted expected total. It tested continuation and reversal after completed volume-clock source moves, with Apex-compatible same-session exits at later expected-volume fractions or 15:30/16:00, and current ES costs. It generated 3,557,450 expanded trade observations and 1,571 positive grouped rows, with zero pass-shaped rows and zero near rows. The best family was short continuation after early downside movement, e.g. 21-day expected volume, 10% to 20% source, 95% expected-volume exit, 24-tick threshold: full n417/PF 1.217/MAR 0.125, core n94/PF 1.354/MAR 1.244, WFA n301/PF 1.535/MAR 0.736/expectancy R 0.235, but incubation n82/PF 0.815/MAR -0.482. Dense early short-continuation rows had WFA n632-741 with PF only 1.34-1.40 and incubation PF near 1.1 or worse. Rejected because volume-clock timing does not satisfy WFA density, WFA PF/MAR/expectancy, and incubation economics together; do not rerun as simple expected-volume-clock continuation, volume-clock reversal, volume-bar timing, or transaction-time proxy without materially new structure or true trade-count/orderflow data.
- Federal Reserve commercial-paper funding-stress screen: rejected before implementation after a narrow near-miss. Source framing: Kacperczyk and Schnabl (2010), "When Safe Proved Risky: Commercial Paper During the Financial Crisis of 2007-2009", Journal of Economic Perspectives 24(1), 29-50, DOI `10.1257/jep.24.1.29`, plus Brunnermeier-Pedersen funding-liquidity logic. Official data source: Federal Reserve Commercial Paper Rates and Outstanding Summary Data Download package `https://www.federalreserve.gov/datadownload/Output.aspx?rel=CP&filetype=zip`; the Fed's CP documentation says issuance rates/volumes are typically updated daily, posted with a one-day lag, and the daily release is usually available at 1:00 p.m. ET. Scratch scripts/results: `/private/tmp/fed_cp_funding_stress_screen.py`, `/private/tmp/fed_cp_funding_stress_screen_top.csv`, `/private/tmp/fed_cp_funding_stress_screen_all.csv`, `/private/tmp/fed_cp_funding_stress_focus.py`, and `/private/tmp/fed_cp_funding_stress_focus_top.csv`; raw official package cached at `/private/tmp/frb_cp.zip`. The no-write screen parsed 4,376 dates and 84 official daily CP rate/volume series from `CP_data.xml`, shifted all CP observations by one business day before ES eligibility, built CP rate levels/changes/ranks/z-scores, A2/P2-minus-AA spreads, financial/asset-backed-minus-nonfinancial spreads, term slopes, and issuance amount/count volume features, then tested Apex-compatible ES RTH long/short holds with current costs. The broad screen evaluated 79,086 positive rows, with zero pass-shaped rows and four near rows. All four near rows used high 63-day rank of total-market 10-20-day CP issuance count (`cp_vol_mkt_10_20_mkt_vol_rank63 >= 0.7`) as a long ES condition. Best flat near row was 09:35-15:59: full n1,143/PF 1.447/MAR 0.291/expectancy R 0.197, core n159/PF 1.739/MAR 2.305, WFA n692/PF 1.480/MAR 0.694/expectancy R 0.214 versus required WFA PF 1.5 and MAR 0.664, and incubation n113/PF 1.552/MAR 1.236. A focused stop-first path audit over nearby thresholds, 09:35-11:00 entries, 15:30/15:59 exits, stop_pct 0.004-0.016, and targets 0.75R-4R produced 2,059 rows, zero pass-shaped rows, and 46 near rows. Best managed row (`threshold=0.7`, 09:35-15:59, `stop_pct=0.016`, `target_r=4.0`) improved drawdown/holdout at full n1,143/PF 1.476/MAR 0.515, core n159/PF 1.622/MAR 2.447, WFA n692/PF 1.451/MAR 0.797/expectancy R 0.202, and incubation n113/PF 1.817/MAR 2.652. Rejected because official CP funding-stress data are reliable and point-in-time usable with a conservative one-business-day lag, but the strongest high-issuance-count long condition misses the WFA PF 1.5 gate before and after path management; do not rerun as simple CP issuance-volume rank, CP rate/spread, A2/P2-minus-AA spread, financial-commercial-paper spread, CP term-slope, or commercial-paper funding-stress filter without materially new structure.

Strongest cluster was morning CVD/large-trade continuation: e.g. `large_trade_pressure_continuation`, `large20_w15_imb0.1`, long 10:00-10:30, n50/net $8,975/PF 2.16/expectancy R 0.465, train PF 2.40, test PF 2.03, positive months 11/13; stricter three-way audit over the top 50 candidates found 29 with PF >=1.2 in 2025 train, 2026-Q1 validation, and 2026-Q2 holdout. Other robust clusters included 10:30 positive 5-minute CVD plus >=8 tick price continuation into 12:00/13:30, 11:00 15-minute pressure continuation, and 13:00/13:30 large-trade pressure fades. Recommendation: purchasing/obtaining longer ES `trades` history is justified for this branch because the signal clusters are simple, repeated, and survive the limited three-way split; however, do not accept or stage a tradable config until a full-history trade-side dataset clears default WFA/monkey/Monte Carlo plus Apex audit. This remains trade-side orderflow only; quote/depth-dependent concepts still require `mbp-1`, `tbbo`, or `mbo`.

The highest-PF rows were sparse 13:30 sell-absorption-long setups, e.g. completed 60-minute `large20_imbalance <= -0.10` with return no worse than -4 ticks, n22/net $5,343/PF 4.75/expectancy R 0.211, but only 3 trades in each 2026 split. Denser rows were unstable: a 10:00 5-minute large-20 sell-absorption-long row reached n44/net $12,668/PF 1.61/expectancy R 0.236, but 2025 train PF was only 1.01 and it stayed below the 50-trade loose gate. Rejected because true trade-side absorption/fade on the available one-year `trades` sample is too sparse or split-unstable; do not promote as simple aggressive-flow absorption, failed-buy fade, failed-sell fade, impact-divergence fade, or large-trade absorption without materially new quote/depth structure or a stronger independent regime filter.

Mechanics: at 10:30 ET trade two-sided continuation only when RTH-open-to-signal price displacement and completed aggregate signed-volume imbalance agree, then flatten at 15:30 ET, before the Gao last-half-hour prediction window. Tunables were capped at two entry params (`min_signal_return_ticks`, `min_orderflow_imbalance`), one stop (`stop_pct`), and one target (`target_r_multiple`). Do not rerun this exact Sierra-compatible morning signed-flow 10:30 1m continuation family as an unknown candidate; use the accepted config/report as the baseline for any production or stress follow-up, not as evidence that Gao's specific last-half-hour dependency passed.

Best visible rows were still negative: signed-flow best net -$50/PF 0.926/MAR -0.073/n10, large20-flow best net -$1,985/PF 0.615/MAR -0.510/n72, and penultimate-alignment best net -$130/PF 0.0/MAR -313/n1.
